<div id="review_1644706816" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644706816" />
    <a title="Ashleyjo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33970054-ashleyjo"><img alt="Ashleyjo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466919724p2/33970054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1644706816?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashleyjo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashleyjo" href="/user/show/33970054-ashleyjo">Ashleyjo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1644706816" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4303889499485431541"><br/>This is honestly one of those books that most readers will see in black or white and either love or hate, which is ironic because the theme of the book is how both emotions can exist so significantly within the same relationship. <br/><br/><b>Anti-hero To The Extreme </b> <br/><br/>Most readers actually like the alpha male character who is a gigantic ass about everything and everyone except for his woman, right? It's the hit man who kills but is a-okay because he saves and loves one woman... The biker who runs drugs and g</span>
  <span id="freeText4303889499485431541" style="display:none"><br>This is honestly one of those books that most readers will see in black or white and either love or hate, which is ironic because the theme of the book is how both emotions can exist so significantly within the same relationship. <br><br><b>Anti-hero To The Extreme </b> <br><br>Most readers actually like the alpha male character who is a gigantic ass about everything and everyone except for his woman, right? It's the hit man who kills but is a-okay because he saves and loves one woman... The biker who runs drugs and guns but is a-okay because he loves one woman? <br><br>Some readers just all out hate the anti-hero character - period. Others... Well, it's easy for readers to accept such a character because the context is small in nature and scale and the victims usually never discussed in depth. <br><br>But, what happens if the context is worldwide vs a biker gang or mob? What happens if the victims are millions vs a few who are easy to imagine as deserving anyway? <br><br>What happens if the dynamic looks more like... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463853062i/19167834._SX540_.jpg" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Or <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463853062i/19167835._SX540_.jpg" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Set Up </b> <br><br>The King has taken anything and everything he wants from the world, Serenity included. Yet, she's the one person he feels has something to offer him that he can't take - true companionship. He's killed millions and left the rest to sickness and famine. Who could love a <i> monster? </i> <br><br>Serenity is the indirect product of the King. Her life has been scavenging, hiding, fighting, &amp; sacrificing. The King has taken everything from her - her parents, her future, her health, her soul. She should hate him. She does hate him. <i>Who </i> could love such a Monster? <br><br><b>Characters </b> <br><br><u> I get Serenity. </u> <br><br><blockquote> "There will be no honor to my sacrifice. Women who have filled the role of temptress have always been looked down upon." </blockquote> <br><br>I almost didn't read this book because a lot of reviews judged her so harshly, and, in my opinion, unfairly. <br><br><blockquote>" I was more likely to punch someone in the face than I was reasoning with them." </blockquote> <br><br>She's mentally and physically strong. She's a fighter, a solider, a diplomat. She's smart. She isn't blinded by loyalty when she thinks the course is wrong. She's self-sacrificing but still values her life. She's jaded by the world, but hasn't written it off. She's a balance of right and wrongs that I can understand and empathize with. <br><br><blockquote>"Where evil is avenged with more evil. It will never be enough to remedy the world." </blockquote> <br><br>Oh, and she's a sarcastic little tart;) <br><br><blockquote>
<br><br>The King : " How do you think I came to rule the world?" <br><br>Serenity : "You're an asshole, and as an asshole, you've done a lot of asshole-ish things - including <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ marrying  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> me. That's how you came to rule the world." <br> </blockquote> <br><br>I don't envy her plight, but I do get it. <br><br><blockquote> "I am Isolde, I am Juliet. I am Guinevere. I am every one of those idiots because I've ..... </blockquote> <br><br><br><u> The King is not so cut and dry for me. </u><br><br><blockquote> "It's not fair that evil can wear such an alluring mask." </blockquote> <br><br>I want to hate him. I do hate him. Yet, I also feel something else for him that I can't quite put my finger on. <br><br><blockquote>"...to cut you up then kiss the wounds he inflicted." </blockquote> <br><br>I can easily see him through Serenity's eyes - the lust, the hate, the resentment, the wonder, the compassion, the need, the confusion, the care. <br><br>Yet, I still have a very difficult time separating the man from the King, the lover from the killer. <br><br>Still, yet, I can easily imagine him cutting his own hand off before he would allow a moment of hurt to touch Serenity. <br><br>The dynamic makes me really ponder historical relationships, such as Eva Braun and Hitler. <br><br><b> Plot </b> <br><br><blockquote>"Wrong is right, and right is wrong." </blockquote> <br><br><b>Bottom Line </b> <br><br>Excellent writing. Excellent plot. Excellent characters. <br><br>That said, I don't think everyone will <i> get</i> this or appreciate it because it's the extreme of the anti-hero plot. <br><br>Off to see how book two goes:) <br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4303889499485431541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2233005408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1414559053575006115">Loved this! I really like reading books with kickass heroines and Serenity fit this role perfectly. She's a soldier fighting to right the wrongs done to her people, her family. She has a lot of hate towards the king and with good reason. <br/><br/>I loved how the king, Montez, wanted Serenity despite her hatred. Nothing she could do would push him away. I love that the king has a dark soul but still had the ability to treat Serenity like a treasure he would protect with everything within him.<br/><br/>I don't norma</span>
  <span id="freeText1414559053575006115" style="display:none">Loved this! I really like reading books with kickass heroines and Serenity fit this role perfectly. She's a soldier fighting to right the wrongs done to her people, her family. She has a lot of hate towards the king and with good reason. <br /><br />I loved how the king, Montez, wanted Serenity despite her hatred. Nothing she could do would push him away. I love that the king has a dark soul but still had the ability to treat Serenity like a treasure he would protect with everything within him.<br /><br />I don't normally enjoy pushing away but I think having Montez's acceptance of her no matter how much she fought him made their verbal sparring exciting. <br /><br />This is a very action packed story and yet the romance is very much the focus. While the king is a darker hero, I wouldn't say this is a very dark story. It does end on a cliffhanger.<br /><br />I listened to the audiobook and would highly recommend it. Laurel Schroeder does a fantastic job of sucking you into Serenity's world and I didn't want it to end.</span>

<div id="review_3552059129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3552059129" />
    <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads"><img alt="NAT.orious reads ☾" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606165351p2/54624224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3552059129?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NAT.orious reads ☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NAT.orious reads ☾" href="/user/show/54624224-nat-orious-reads">NAT.orious reads ☾</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3552059129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15933318989648589003"><u>
  <b>4 STARS, as surprised as you are ★★★★✩</b>
</u><br/><i>
  <blockquote>
<b>This book is for you if… </b>you’ve not yet found a book of the Stockholm-syndrome-induced-Romance that fits your taste but are still willing to give the genre a try. (Let's not talk about how weird that desire is in general.) I was SO ready to be all judgemental about this book but my will had to face defeat far quicker than I’d like to admit.</blockquote>
</i><br/><b>⤐ <i>Overall.</i></b><br/>Strictly speaking, <i>The Queen of All that Dies</i> does not sort itself into the genre of dark romance. Ho</span>
  <span id="freeText15933318989648589003" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>4 STARS, as surprised as you are ★★★★✩</b>
</u><br><i>
  <blockquote>
<b>This book is for you if… </b>you’ve not yet found a book of the Stockholm-syndrome-induced-Romance that fits your taste but are still willing to give the genre a try. (Let's not talk about how weird that desire is in general.) I was SO ready to be all judgemental about this book but my will had to face defeat far quicker than I’d like to admit.</blockquote>
</i><br><b>⤐ <i>Overall.</i></b><br>Strictly speaking, <i>The Queen of All that Dies</i> does not sort itself into the genre of dark romance. However, if the relationship between the love interests is determined mainly by one abducting/buying the other in a trade, the groundwork is pretty solid in my eyes.<br><br>Naturally, I was ready to bash this book like a pinata. But the <b>slow shift of both Serenity's and her superiors' alliances was extremely intriguing</b>. I loved how the <b>line between good and bad began to blurr</b> until it seemed to be barely there anymore. Although, undoubtedly, Montez is the evilest man in this game of thrones, others come quite close which is the reason I was so hot and bothered for his and Serenetiy's relationship to develop.<br><br>If I had to pick one thing I deeply disliked, I'd definitely say the most unbearable aspect of this audiobook was the <b>excrutiating French/Swiss German accent</b> the narrator chose for Montez. I can see where the reasoning behind that might be coming from. Thing is, this accent is about as sexy as a date in between the confinements of an insect farm. In case my - admittedly, imperfect metaphor/simile - doesn't quite catch: NOT SEXY. NOT AT ALL.<br><br>Which made the idea of Montez as the sexy overlord of the world appear very foreign to me. I might be going out on a limb here, but if one is able to conquer the entire world, I expect him to conquer at least some sort of standard English along side of it. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600784113ra/30139359.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>⤐ <i>What’s happening.</i></b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘‘You were able to kill him,’ Will said. You, a girl. That’s what he meant. Like owning a vagina made me inferior in some fundamental way.’</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Serenity knows nothing but fight and kill. Her organisation of states - the WUN - is the last thing standing between the King Montez Lazuli and his regiency over the entire globe. When she is sent to negotiate the peace talks alongside her father, she realises two things:<br><blockquote>1. her superiors sending her there was not out of shortage of adequate staff<br>2. she's not as immune to the man who killed her mother as she thought she would be3. her functioning as bait for the King to take in exchange for what the WUN want from the negotiations is working...</blockquote><br>_____________________<br><b>4 STARS.</b><i> Would stay up beyond my typical hours to finish it. I found some minor details I didn't like, agree with or lacked in some kind but overall, this was enjoyable and extraordinary. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15933318989648589003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2459963692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2459963692" />
    <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy"><img alt="Stacey is Sassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474185067p2/12062194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2459963692?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey is Sassy" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy">Stacey is Sassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24384663-the-queen-of-all-that-dies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=she-kicks-butt">she-kicks-butt</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=angry-fix">angry-fix</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=cranky-hero">cranky-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=mind-f">mind-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=is-that-a-gun-in-your-pocket">is-that-a-gun-in-your-pocket</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=there-will-be-blood">there-will-be-blood</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2459963692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2053055480568339494"><b>The war is over, and your enemy is now your husband...</b><br/><br/>Goh BLIMEY!! <i>Laura Thalassa</i> really knows how to sock it to you. <i>The Queen of All that Dies</i> was fantastic. I think her writing is original but it affects me in a different way to other stories. I find myself a constant observer. When I read a lot of my other books, I place myself in the heroine's position. I am fighting, working, dancing and living as the heroine. I live and breathe their lives from the first page to the last. When I read a <i>La</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2053055480568339494" style="display:none"><b>The war is over, and your enemy is now your husband...</b><br><br>Goh BLIMEY!! <i>Laura Thalassa</i> really knows how to sock it to you. <i>The Queen of All that Dies</i> was fantastic. I think her writing is original but it affects me in a different way to other stories. I find myself a constant observer. When I read a lot of my other books, I place myself in the heroine's position. I am fighting, working, dancing and living as the heroine. I live and breathe their lives from the first page to the last. When I read a <i>Laura Thalassa</i>, I can't quite step into the heroine's shoes. Her shoes are too big for me to wear. I can't be the strong, determined, kick arse...detached, mechanical and ruthless heroine I meet. I must stand at her side with my hands tied to my sides... watching, observing... hiding.<br><br>I found myself gutted by the situation Serenity was forced into. Serenity was a pawn. Serenity was a gift. Serenity must forsake her own happiness to end a war. She must knowingly walk into a trap, smile and graciously accept that she has been offered up as a sacrifice to end a war. Serenity has been handed over to a King, a King that is the cause of all her misery.<br><br>But, the murderer of many has a weakness. Turns out, all that was needed to bring about his downfall was Serenity.<br><br>It's a funny thing reading this book. You know that King Lazuli is the worst, most evil man on earth. He's killed a lot of people, ruined the world and the environment, all while living in the lap of luxury. It was hard to see only the bad though. Like Serenity, I see the touches of humanity, vulnerability and emotion he can't hide. There's passion in his eyes when he looks at Serenity. He will do anything to keep her safe and protect her from harm. He wants her love and he's doing everything in his power to get it. BUT...I have to keep reminding myself HE'S BAD!!<br><br>I am absolutely STOKED that this series is already out. For the first time EVER, I loved that this one had a cliffy ending. It ended in a way that left me hungering for more. It was interesting, I didn't see it coming and I was left thoroughly satisfied AND I DON'T HAVE TO WAIT FOR MORE!!!<br><br>If you haven't tried a <i>Laura Thalassa</i>, I suggest you get to it. Sure, they're a touch confronting and it's bloody hard work falling for the heroes, but her words are so interesting. The books I've tried so far has been excellent. They're fresh, interesting, thought-provoking, sexy and intriguing. Exactly what I look for in my reads. I'm looking for <i>Traitors</i> in <i>The Fallen World #2</i><br><br><a href="http://staceyissassy.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475811106i/20768637._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><a href="http://staceyissassy.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502607237i/23575101.jpg" width="570" height="170" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/StaceyisSassy/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004243.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://www.pinterest.com/Stacey1565/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004244.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://www.twitter.com/StaceyisSassy" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004245.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2720462147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8817636554555654598">Wow! This book immediately pulled me in and held me, sometimes by the throat. There is so much here and all of it written in such a way that I felt as if I too were a part of this world along with Serenity. She is one hardcore heroine, raised out of necessity to be a soldier, trained to become emissary upon the death of her father. Her world is a dark and despairing place with little to no hope. And now her country is depending on her to negotiate peace with the man who is responsible for all th</span>
  <span id="freeText8817636554555654598" style="display:none">Wow! This book immediately pulled me in and held me, sometimes by the throat. There is so much here and all of it written in such a way that I felt as if I too were a part of this world along with Serenity. She is one hardcore heroine, raised out of necessity to be a soldier, trained to become emissary upon the death of her father. Her world is a dark and despairing place with little to no hope. And now her country is depending on her to negotiate peace with the man who is responsible for all the destruction she has borne witness to. <br /><br />This story starts out fast and it never slows down. The romance here is heavily laced with action and political intrigue which resulted in a pulse pounding experience. Martes, the king, is such a multi-dimensional character. While I knew exactly what and who Serenity was, I hungered to know more about the king. We are given bits of his thoughts and through them it was apparent he was so much more than what is seen on the surface. My romantic heart thrilled at his almost instant want of the heroine, at his protectiveness of her. And yet, I screamed along with Serenity when truths about him were brought into the light. In the midst of all the turmoil was her feelings towards him which are muddled and confused. I sympathized with her completely.<br /><br />This ends on one doozy of a cliffhanger. With some of Martes’ secrets revealed, there are still so many more things that these characters must find solutions for. Fortunately, all the books in this trilogy are now available and will be diving into book 2 immediately.<br /><br />Read via Kindle Unlimited<br />Mostly heroine pov although there are some from the hero<br />Safe <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[no ow drama – H not made out to be a manwhore; h is a virgin; om drama caused by a fellow soldier that the h grew up with – he leads the resistance <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Triggers <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[violence; attempted rape but only the mention of it having been planned – h prevented it from happening <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

    <a title="Didi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082482-didi"><img alt="Didi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459297426p2/6082482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1208299741?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Didi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Didi" href="/user/show/6082482-didi">Didi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24384663-the-queen-of-all-that-dies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=tragic-loss">tragic-loss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=his-pov">his-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1208299741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9683863917664354799">That was really good! I loved it! <br/><br/>New adult dystopian romance, is what I'd call this. It was better than what I was expecting and had me glued to the pages. I loved seeing years of planned revenge wilt in the midst of new knowledge and the promise of love. Serenity was a soldier raised to hate the king and all he was responsible for destroying. The world as we know it no longer exists. It's fractured into the western and eastern hemispheres with all the countries either having surrendered or bee</span>
  <span id="freeText9683863917664354799" style="display:none">That was really good! I loved it! <br /><br />New adult dystopian romance, is what I'd call this. It was better than what I was expecting and had me glued to the pages. I loved seeing years of planned revenge wilt in the midst of new knowledge and the promise of love. Serenity was a soldier raised to hate the king and all he was responsible for destroying. The world as we know it no longer exists. It's fractured into the western and eastern hemispheres with all the countries either having surrendered or been captured by the Kings regime. Serenity lives in what was once the U.S, but now is part of the WUN--Western United Nations, encompassing north and South America. When she is sent on a mission for peace with her father, she senses the futile repercussions of meeting the man who now rules the world and controls her fear.<br /><br />King Montes Lazuli is an enigma. He's shrouded in mystery and his life rumored to be immortal. But when he meets Serenity everything changes. What once was wrong becomes right, what once was ethical becomes questionable. I loved seeing both sides of the king. The side the world sees, as a ruthless leader, and the side Serenity sees, a compassionate and loving kindred spirit. <br />This is filled with action, betrayal, mystery and an unlikely romance. There were several times I was gasping over the turn of events. It was very stressful for Serenity to be raised a certain way then see all her closely held values come into question. I also loved seeing how the king was with her. He was in desperate need for someone like Serenity and watching him protect and honor her was sweet.<br /><br />This of course ends on a mother cliffy! And then I see the sequel doesn't release till January 2016?! SAY WHAT?!<br />The book never dragged and kept me interested for every second I read. I can't wait to see what happens, I just wish it wasn't so far away! </span>
  <a data-text-id="9683863917664354799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24384663-the-queen-of-all-that-dies">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1609384414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17079619269664355650">I've read some crazy, ignorant stuff before, but never as bad as "The Queen of All that Dies." It was laughable to say the least. The author clearly didn't conduct any research for this novel, nor common sense, nor basic dystopian 101. I mean, I don't even know where to begin with this. I guess the writing is a good start. <br/><br/><u>Writing:</u><br/>The writing was fine, if you enjoy fanfics. That's how it flowed to me. Like most fanfics, there's usually no logic or common sense when it comes to them. They're usua</span>
  <span id="freeText17079619269664355650" style="display:none">I've read some crazy, ignorant stuff before, but never as bad as "The Queen of All that Dies." It was laughable to say the least. The author clearly didn't conduct any research for this novel, nor common sense, nor basic dystopian 101. I mean, I don't even know where to begin with this. I guess the writing is a good start. <br /><br /><u>Writing:</u><br />The writing was fine, if you enjoy fanfics. That's how it flowed to me. Like most fanfics, there's usually no logic or common sense when it comes to them. They're usually solely about the romance between the main characters, thus being the cause the authors', I guess don't see a point in world building or fact checking for their work. Now, I'm sure there might be a quality fanfic out there, but I have yet to read it. <br /><br /><u>Plot:</u><br />The plot sounded so promising to me. A war torn Earth, destroyed and ruled by a undying king, and a resistance that will stop at nothing to see him dead even going as far to use one of their own as a pawn in the game of power. Sounds cool, right? I was expecting some epic action scenes, a well written villain that I love to hate, and some awesome world building. What I got was some half baked killing scenes, a wimpy and spoiled king, and very weak world building. The author obviously didn't do any research for this novel because it made no sense. First off, Serenity lives dab smack in one of the areas a nuclear bomb was dropped, and some how, she's still alive. Any place that a bomb of that much power would land, would not be livable for a very long time, if ever. The air wouldn't be breathable, there would be too much radiation, and anything that once grew, would be incapable of doing so. It also wouldn't just effect one area, it would cause a catastrophe on most of the planet, if not all. Another thing that bothered me was a lack dystopian info. If something like a nuclear bomb or a tyrant king destroyed some place on this earth, I sure as hell wouldn't be walking around wearing dresses, high heels, and, <i>makeup</i>. Yes, Serenity actually parades around in this when she goes to meet the king all the way until the end of the book. Like, where did they even find the material and products and resources to even make that happen?! And I would think they would have more important things to think about. Like surviving. There was also things like working cars, limos, swimming pools, very advanced technology that has no science behind it, dinner dates that you would have in today's time and day, not in a dystopian world. So, basically I was a confused person during reading this novel. <br /><br /><u>Characters:</u><br />Alright, let's talk about my least favorite character; Montes.... the king of Geneva. He's one of the worst anti-heroes I have ever had the displeasure of reading about. He's suppose to be this heartless, cruel king that's killed millions of people without a second thought, but what he comes across as is a spoiled, creepy, psychotic, wimpy, possessive asshole that hides behind his soldiers' and they're not even soldiers! They're like his personal body guards. He also has killed millions of people... I can't justify him for that, I can't see how anyone could. He's a killer that makes other men do his dirty work and calls himself powerful. Then there's Serenity. I don't have much to say about her, she was an okay character, until she went and got Stockholm Syndrome her Montes because I'm not calling it "love" when it's anything but. <br /><br /><u>Romance:</u><br />The romance was terrible. First, he's like 60, okay? He just doesn't look it and usually I'm okay with this if it's in fantasy or something paranormal, but when he has to take pills to keep him from aging, that's a whole other ball park. That's creepy. She's only 19. Through the whole novel, Montes is always pushing and forcing Serenity into situations she doesn't want to be in. From the very first moment that lay eyes on each other "he just has to have her." *insert eye roll* and does he ever. Because he forces her to be with him. Serenity's feelings for the king range from hate and repulsion, but not love, maybe lust sometimes, but nothing that would give him the okay to force her to marry him, have sex when him when he can clearly see she doesn't want to, that her body and mind isn't in it 100% and she hasn't given her consent. She literally tells him she hates him during their sex scenes... this is rape and I'm not okay with it. If ones partner isn't it emotionally, physically, or mentally in it, you better step away, buddy. He's never hit her before, but there's another form of abuse and that's mentally and emotionally, the kind of abuse the king hands out to Serenity. So, yeah, I loathe his character and I loathe the romance between them when it was so sallow and wrong. <br /><br /><u>Conclusion:</u><br />I know this was long, but I had to get out all my feels, my raging feels. I don't recommended this book to anyone and caution you not to even touch it with a ten foot pole. But if you're looking for a published like fanfic, a creepy, rapey king, and a romance that makes you wanna gag, this is the book for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17079619269664355650" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7709400036557298721">This genre is not really my thing but I could see a YA audience digging it. I don't have a problem with anti-heroes or unlikable, even villainous characters because they are often more interesting than the self-righteous do-gooding Mary Sues of the World. My problem with this book was that it was too superficial for me, with the characters making drastic about-faces at a dizzying pace. I couldn't take the story seriously or lose myself in it, nor was I invested in any of the characters. It was j</span>
  <span id="freeText7709400036557298721" style="display:none">This genre is not really my thing but I could see a YA audience digging it. I don't have a problem with anti-heroes or unlikable, even villainous characters because they are often more interesting than the self-righteous do-gooding Mary Sues of the World. My problem with this book was that it was too superficial for me, with the characters making drastic about-faces at a dizzying pace. I couldn't take the story seriously or lose myself in it, nor was I invested in any of the characters. It was just an entertaining, quick read that is outside my norm. I appreciated the ideas that the author had and was trying to get across. In the hands of a more seasoned writer, fleshing out characters and plot, this could have been a Hunger Game type book.</span>

<div id="review_3097562876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3097562876" />
    <a title="Susan&#39;s Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19736308-susan-s-reviews"><img alt="Susan&#39;s Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507651790p2/19736308.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3097562876?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan&#39;s Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan&#39;s Reviews" href="/user/show/19736308-susan-s-reviews">Susan&#39;s Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3097562876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15094639230425026095">So! I'm not into fantasy or sci fi, but once in a while, I don't mind the odd dystopian novel. The only draw-back is that this is a three book series. Inevitably, the amount of filler in each book just drags the story down. Things get repetitive, then I start to lose interest. <br/><br/>The first novel was pretty riveting, although Serenity's physical attraction to the brutal king could have been fleshed out a bit more to make it more believable. She sees her own brutal nature in him - we are told this re</span>
  <span id="freeText15094639230425026095" style="display:none">So! I'm not into fantasy or sci fi, but once in a while, I don't mind the odd dystopian novel. The only draw-back is that this is a three book series. Inevitably, the amount of filler in each book just drags the story down. Things get repetitive, then I start to lose interest. <br /><br />The first novel was pretty riveting, although Serenity's physical attraction to the brutal king could have been fleshed out a bit more to make it more believable. She sees her own brutal nature in him - we are told this repeatedly. However, once Serenity "did her duty" in order to save her country, the relationship aspect became a bit more believable: Serenity could see that the King was just as lonely (and ruthless) as she was. Somewhere inside that handsome shell, Serenity sensed that the King had some redeeming characteristics, which she intended on manipulating to her war torn country's favor. Serenity is no victim: she fully intends to use her position to end the war that is plaguing the world.<br /><br />In the second installment of this series, Serenity started behaving like an emotional ping pong ball. She loves the Monster, she hates the Monster, and so on and so forth. I still managed to enjoy this story, but decided to give the final installment a pass almost half way through. Four hundred plus pages of more emotional ping pong? I don't think so.<br /><br />This year, I'm trying to avoid addictive habits, and serialized novels involving the same main characters is one of those addictive habits I'm passing on in 2020. I might make allowances for a second installment, but I'm going to be very choosy in my lapses. Some things need to end: time to move on to another melodrama!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15094639230425026095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1883770100" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1883770100" />
    <a title="Kaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35924884-kaila"><img alt="Kaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533304308p2/35924884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1883770100?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaila" href="/user/show/35924884-kaila">Kaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24384663-the-queen-of-all-that-dies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=heroine-needs-to-be-slapped">heroine-needs-to-be-slapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=trigger-warning-abuse-or-rape">trigger-warning-abuse-or-rape</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=arranged-or-forced-marriage">arranged-or-forced-marriage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=hate-to-love">hate-to-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35924884-kaila?shelf=morally-ambiguous">morally-ambiguous</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1883770100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7391220128112505752"><blockquote>
  <b>“Once upon a time we were innocent, and then we were not.” </b>
</blockquote> <br/> <br/><b>2.5/5 stars</b> <br/><br/>I'm really conflicted about this book. I definitely didn't like it and this was established from the start, but I also can't say that I totally didn't enjoy it. Especially towards the end, action was picking up, twists were being revealed and the romantic tension was boiling over...and it was all so entertaining. Do you see my predicament, I didn't particularly like it but I also found it entertaining...I'm just very co</span>
  <span id="freeText7391220128112505752" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“Once upon a time we were innocent, and then we were not.” </b>
</blockquote> <br> <br><b>2.5/5 stars</b> <br><br>I'm really conflicted about this book. I definitely didn't like it and this was established from the start, but I also can't say that I totally didn't enjoy it. Especially towards the end, action was picking up, twists were being revealed and the romantic tension was boiling over...and it was all so entertaining. Do you see my predicament, I didn't particularly like it but I also found it entertaining...I'm just very confused.<br><br>I'm going to try and not be sarcastic when explaining the plot, but it is a little ridiculous so it'll be hard.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491059731i/22372647.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a dystopian novel set in a war-torn world in the future. King Lazuri of the Eastern Empire has conquered the world and is cunning, seemingly immortal, ruthless and pure evil...especially to the people of the defeated WUN (Western United Nations). Living in a world where she has had to kill to survive, Serenity has known all the hardships that war has brought and she blames it all on the king. <br><br>With her father, she has been chosen to represent the WUN with peace agreements with the Eastern Empire. Except, she also knows the real reason for her being there: to seduce the king. King Lazuri wants her as soon as they meet, but Serenity can't seem to forgive all the pain that he is caused her and her family. But in order to save her nation, Serenity must sacrifice herself and perhaps even surrender her heart to the king. <br><br>I'm not going to go in too much detail about what I don't like because I have been known to rant, and in that case I will be here for hours.<br><b>What I especially didn't enjoy:</b><br><br><b>The overall unbelievability of the story:</b>This book was focused on the romance which was very cliche and unbelievable. He sees her once and suddenly knows that he has to have her, will give up his life for her and instantly stops being an awful, evil tyrant because of their 'connection'. I don't think so.<br><br><b>Romanticised abuse:</b> Having sex with someone you hate and not enjoying the experience (whilst still having the physical pleasures of sex) against your will. Call my unromantic but that seems an awful lot like...sexual abuse. In saying this, later in in the story the sex wasn't like this at all and it was only the first one or so times. But this doesn't forgive the fact that unrequited sexual acts were seriously romanticised and played off as intense and emotional love scenes!<br><br><b>The main character's blatant hate of women.</b> I understand that she didn't like dresses, jewellery or make up (trust me, we were told one hundred times) but did she have to then go and hate all the other women in the book. What was worse is the author wrote her to be a feminist because she was badass and could kill people, but in reality she was so anti-woman! And, on top of that, I think she was one of the only named female character and she was definitely the only main female character. I reckon I could count on one hand the amount of times another main female was present and actively contributing to the story. <br><br>There are more, but I think you get the idea.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“You want to see compassion? Fine." I take the hand pressed against my shoulders and kiss his knuckles. "I've now kissed the hand of my mother's killer."<br>Before he has time to react to my chaste kiss, I bring my other hand up and slap him. His head whips to the side.<br>"I'm also a vindictive bitch," I say</b>
</blockquote><br><br>What I did enjoy:<br><br><b>Fast-paced excitement: </b>Now, with that list above it may seem like I hated the book, but I don't. I normally don't pick up on problematic themes and ideas in books and even if I do, I can still enjoy a story no matter how bad these themes get. This was the case in this book. I think it portrayed many negative ideals but it was also entertaining as heck. There was constant action, political intrigue and twists that kept the story exciting. That cliffhanger ending makes me want to pick up the next book immediately because I just have to know what's happening next!<br><br><b>Angsty romance: </b>I'm a hopeless romantic, so any sort of tension-filled and hate yo love relationship makes my heart swell. I don't particularly like it at the start but as the story progresses, I was just dying for the pair to get together. It started getting more romantic and angsty as the book progressed and I was totally there for it. Plus, The King was completely humbled by Serenity and there was definitely lots of sweetness on his behalf to try and win her over, which was just an added bonus.<br><br>In all, I can't say that the good outweighs the bad but I am excited for the next book and enjoyed the overall story, no matter how problematic it was.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I stare into the king’s eyes. I am Isolde, I am Juliet, I am Guinevere. I am every one of those idiots because I’ve fallen for the king.” </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7391220128112505752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13770875065005937180">There were times that I thought this book had potential to be REALLY good and other times that had my eyes rolling at the silliness of it all. The dialogue felt off throughout the entirety, and I never understood the connection the 60 year old king of the chiseled abs felt with the barely adult Serenity, who could sneer people into terror with her ever so frightening stare and scar. BUT, and there is a but, even with the overall eyeroll-worthiness I still read it from beginning to end and will p</span>
  <span id="freeText13770875065005937180" style="display:none">There were times that I thought this book had potential to be REALLY good and other times that had my eyes rolling at the silliness of it all. The dialogue felt off throughout the entirety, and I never understood the connection the 60 year old king of the chiseled abs felt with the barely adult Serenity, who could sneer people into terror with her ever so frightening stare and scar. BUT, and there is a but, even with the overall eyeroll-worthiness I still read it from beginning to end and will probably read the next one.</span>

		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1JpIJJtxOFiCnooBK84LawmHiRgZCE84LGbxCDvbtJvfWItPtVdKcPBdu+6SOi1SMWj2vLe1iM05yDnqTq5Dng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('64LYBCKNJjPOqufpzELhnkioZAO5/McFk0RkS0lke03gQBtvDKtUG7xp1gZ1tsencEcbpxdBAPCG6qypPBGMSA==')})
  }
//]]>
